href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Land_%26_Armaments" title="BAE Systems Land &amp; Armaments">BAE Systems Land &amp; Armaments</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height:1.35em;">\n<span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://baesystems.com">baesystems<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>BAE Systems plc</b> is a British <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational</a> <a href="/wiki/Arms_industry" title="Arms industry">defence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Information_security" title="Information security">security</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Aerospace" title="Aerospace">aerospace</a> company. Its headquarters are in London in the United Kingdom and it has operations worldwide. It is among the world\'s largest defence companies; it was ranked as the third-largest based on applicable 2015 revenues.<sup id="cite_ref-DefenseNews_Top_100_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DefenseNews_Top_100-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>  Its largest operations are in the United Kingdom and United States, where its <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Inc." title="BAE Systems Inc.">BAE Systems Inc.</a> subsidiary is one of the six largest suppliers to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">US Department of Defense</a>. Other major markets include Australia, India, and Saudi Arabia, which account for about 20% of BAE\'s overall sales.<sup id="cite_ref-veconomist_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-veconomist-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> It is the biggest manufacturer in Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-veconomist_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-veconomist-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The company was formed on 30 November 1999 by the <a href="/wiki/British_pound_sterling" class="mw-redirect" title="British pound sterling">\xc2\xa3</a>7.7&#160;billion merger of two British companies: <a href="/wiki/Marconi_Electronic_Systems" title="Marconi Electronic Systems">Marconi Electronic Systems</a> (MES) \xe2\x80\x93 the defence electronics and naval shipbuilding subsidiary of the <a href="/wiki/General_Electric_Company_plc" class="mw-redirect" title="General Electric Company plc">General Electric Company plc</a> (GEC) \xe2\x80\x93 and <a href="/wiki/British_Aerospace" title="British Aerospace">British Aerospace</a> (BAe) \xe2\x80\x93 an aircraft, munitions and naval systems manufacturer.\n</p><p>BAE Systems is the successor to various aircraft, shipbuilding, armoured vehicle, armaments and defence electronics companies, including the <a href="/wiki/Marconi_Company" title="Marconi Company">Marconi Company</a>, the first commercial company devoted to the development and use of radio; <a href="/wiki/Avro" title="Avro">A.V. Roe and Company</a>, one of the world\'s first aircraft companies; <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland" title="De Havilland">de Havilland</a>, manufacturer of the  <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Comet" title="De Havilland Comet">Comet</a>, the world\'s first commercial jet airliner; <a href="/wiki/British_Aircraft_Corporation" title="British Aircraft Corporation">British Aircraft Corporation</a>, co-manufacturer of the <a href="/wiki/Concorde" title="Concorde">Concorde</a> supersonic transport; <a href="/wiki/Supermarine" title="Supermarine">Supermarine</a>, manufacturer of the <a href="/wiki/Supermarine_Spitfire" title="Supermarine Spitfire">Spitfire</a>; <a href="/wiki/Yarrow_Shipbuilders" title="Yarrow Shipbuilders">Yarrow Shipbuilders</a>, builder of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Havock_class_destroyer" class="mw-redirect" title="Havock class destroyer">first destroyers</a>; <a href="/wiki/Fairfield_Shipbuilding_and_Engineering_Company" title="Fairfield Shipbuilding and Engineering Company">Fairfield Shipbuilding and Engineering Company</a>, pioneer of the <a href="/wiki/Triple-expansion_engine" class="mw-redirect" title="Triple-expansion engine">triple-expansion engine</a> and builder of the world\'s first <a href="/wiki/Invincible-class_battlecruiser" title="Invincible-class battlecruiser">battlecruiser</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Shipbuilding_and_Engineering" title="Vickers Shipbuilding and Engineering">Vickers Shipbuilding and Engineering</a>, builder of the Royal Navy\'s first <a href="/wiki/Holland_class_submarine" class="mw-redirect" title="Holland class submarine">submarines</a>. Since its formation it has made a number of acquisitions, most notably of <a href="/wiki/United_Defense" title="United Defense">United Defense</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armor_Holdings" title="Armor Holdings">Armor Holdings</a> of the United States, and sold its shares in <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Astrium" title="Astrium">Astrium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alenia_Marconi_Systems" title="Alenia Marconi Systems">AMS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atlas_Elektronik" title="Atlas Elektronik">Atlas Elektronik</a>.\n</p><p>BAE Systems is involved in several major defence projects, including the <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin_F-35_Lightning_II" title="Lockheed Martin F-35 Lightning II">Lockheed Martin F-35 Lightning II</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eurofighter_Typhoon" title="Eurofighter Typhoon">Eurofighter Typhoon</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Astute-class_submarine" title="Astute-class submarine"><i>Astute</i>-class</a> <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarine</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Queen Elizabeth-class aircraft carrier"><i>Queen Elizabeth</i>-class</a> <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carriers</a>. BAE Systems is listed on the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a> and is a constituent of the <a href="/wiki/FTSE_100_Index" title="FTSE 100 Index">FTSE 100 Index</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Espionage"><span class="tocnumber">9.1</span> <span class="toctext">Espionage</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a class="toctext">Saudi war crimes in Yemen</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Political_influence"><span class="tocnumber">9.5</span> <span class="toctext">Political influence</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Heritage">Heritage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Heritage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Spitfire_VII_Langley_USA.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Spitfire_VII_Langley_USA.jpg/220px-Spitfire_VII_Langley_USA.jpg" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Spitfire_VII_Langley_USA.jpg/330px-Spitfire_VII_Langley_USA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Spitfire_VII_Langley_USA.jpg/440px-Spitfire_VII_Langley_USA.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1561" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spitfire_VII_Langley_USA.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Supermarine" title="Supermarine">Supermarine</a>, the manufacturer of the <a href="/wiki/Supermarine_Spitfire" title="Supermarine Spitfire">Spitfire</a> was a predecessor company of BAE Systems. It was purchased by <a href="/wiki/Vickers-Armstrongs" title="Vickers-Armstrongs">Vickers-Armstrongs</a>, which itself was merged into the <a href="/wiki/British_Aircraft_Corporation" title="British Aircraft Corporation">British Aircraft Corporation</a> in 1960.</div></div></div>\n<p>BAE Systems was formed on 30 November 1999 by the \xc2\xa37.7&#160;billion merger of British Aerospace (BAe) and Marconi Electronic Systems (MES).<sup id="cite_ref-scotsman2000_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scotsman2000-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> As a result, BAE Systems is the successor to many of the most famous British aircraft, defence electronics and warship manufacturers. Predecessor companies built the <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Comet" title="De Havilland Comet">Comet</a>, the world\'s first commercial jet airliner; the <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Siddeley_Harrier" title="Hawker Siddeley Harrier">Harrier</a> "jump jet", the world\'s first operational <a href="/wiki/V/STOL" title="V/STOL">Vertical/Short Take-Off and Landing</a> (VTOL) aircraft; the "groundbreaking"<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Blue Vixen radar carried by <a href="/wiki/BAE_Sea_Harrier#Specifications_(Sea_Harrier_FA2)" class="mw-redirect" title="BAE Sea Harrier">Sea Harrier FA2s</a> and which formed the basis of the Eurofighter\'s <a href="/wiki/Euroradar_CAPTOR" title="Euroradar CAPTOR">CAPTOR</a> radar; and co-produced the iconic <a href="/wiki/Concorde" title="Concorde">Concorde</a> supersonic airliner with <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9rospatiale" title="A\xc3\xa9rospatiale">A\xc3\xa9rospatiale</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>British Aerospace was a civil and <a href="/wiki/Military_aircraft" title="Military aircraft">military aircraft</a> manufacturer, as well as a provider of military land systems. The company had emerged from the massive consolidation of UK aircraft manufacturers since World War II. British Aerospace was formed on 29 April 1977 by the nationalisation and merger of The <a href="/wiki/British_Aircraft_Corporation" title="British Aircraft Corporation">British Aircraft Corporation</a> (BAC), the <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Siddeley" title="Hawker Siddeley">Hawker Siddeley Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Aviation" title="Scottish Aviation">Scottish Aviation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-compcomm_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-compcomm-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Both BAC and Hawker Siddeley were themselves the result of various mergers and acquisitions.<sup id="cite_ref-lineage_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lineage-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Marconi Electronic Systems was the defence subsidiary of British engineering firm The General Electric Company (GEC), dealing largely in military <a href="/wiki/System_integrator" class="mw-redirect" title="System integrator">systems integration</a>, as well as naval and land systems. Marconi\'s heritage dates back to <a href="/wiki/Guglielmo_Marconi" title="Guglielmo Marconi">Guglielmo Marconi</a>\'s Wireless Telegraph &amp; Signal Company, founded in 1897.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> GEC purchased <a href="/wiki/English_Electric" title="English Electric">English Electric</a> (which included Marconi) in 1968 and thereafter used the Marconi brand for its defence businesses (as GEC-Marconi and later Marconi Electronic Systems). GEC\'s own defence heritage dates back to World War I, when its contribution to the war effort included radios and bulbs. World War II consolidated this position, as the company was involved in important technological advances, notably the <a href="/wiki/Cavity_magnetron" title="Cavity magnetron">cavity magnetron</a> for <a href="/wiki/Radar" title="Radar">radar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Between 1945 and 1999, GEC-Marconi/Marconi Electronic Systems became one of the world\'s most important <a href="/wiki/Defence_contractor" class="mw-redirect" title="Defence contractor">defence contractors</a>. GEC\'s major defence related acquisitions included <a href="/wiki/Associated_Electrical_Industries" title="Associated Electrical Industries">Associated Electrical Industries</a> in 1967,<sup id="cite_ref-cc_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cc-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yarrow_Shipbuilders_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="Yarrow Shipbuilders Limited">Yarrow Shipbuilders</a> in 1985,<sup id="cite_ref-cc_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cc-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Plessey" title="Plessey">Plessey</a> companies in 1989,<sup id="cite_ref-plesseyferranti_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plesseyferranti-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> parts of <a href="/wiki/Ferranti" title="Ferranti">Ferranti</a>\'s defence business in 1990,<sup id="cite_ref-plesseyferranti_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plesseyferranti-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> the rump of <a href="/wiki/Ferranti" title="Ferranti">Ferranti</a> when it went into receivership in 1993/1994, <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Shipbuilding_and_Engineering" title="Vickers Shipbuilding and Engineering">Vickers Shipbuilding and Engineering</a> in 1995<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Kvaerner_Govan" title="Kvaerner Govan">Kv\xc3\xa6rner Govan</a> in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In June 1998, MES acquired <a href="/wiki/Tracor" title="Tracor">Tracor</a>, a major American defence contractor, for \xc2\xa3830&#160;million (approx. US$1.4&#160;billion c. 1998).<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="navbox collapsible autocollapse">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th width="2%">6</td>\n<td width="2%">7</td>\n<td width="2%">8</td>\n<td width="2%">9\n</td>\n<td width="2%">0</td>\n<td width="2%">1</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="10" width="20%" style="text-align:center;background-color:#F0F0F0;">1960s\n</td>\n<td colspan="10" width="20%" style="text-align:center;background-color:#F0F0F0;">1970s\n</td>\n<td colspan="10" width="20%" style="text-align:center;background-color:#F0F0F0;">1980s\n</td>\n<td colspan="10" width="20%" style="text-align:center;background-color:#F0F0F0;">1990s\n</td>\n<td colspan="10" width="20%" style="text-align:center;background-color:#F0F0F0;">2000s\n</td>\n<td colspan="10" width="20%" style="text-align:center;background-color:#F0F0F0;">2010s\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;font-size:100%; color:#7ec0ee">\n<td colspan="50"><span style="text-decoration:none;background-color:#7EC0EE;">BSC</span> <span style="text-decoration:none;color:#000000;"><b>= <a href="/wiki/British_Shipbuilders" title="British Shipbuilders">British Shipbuilders Corporation</a></b></span>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formation">Formation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Formation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The 1997 merger of American corporations <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a> and <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas" title="McDonnell Douglas">McDonnell Douglas</a>, which followed the forming of <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">Lockheed Martin</a>, the world\'s largest defence contractor in 1995, increased the pressure on European defence companies to consolidate. In June 1997 British Aerospace Defence managing director <a href="/wiki/John_Weston_(businessman)" title="John Weston (businessman)">John Weston</a> commented "Europe... is supporting three times the number of contractors on less than half the budget of the U.S.".<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> European governments wished to see the merger of their defence manufacturers into a single entity, a European Aerospace and Defence Company.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As early as 1995 British Aerospace and the German aerospace and defence company <a href="/wiki/DaimlerChrysler_Aerospace" class="mw-redirect" title="DaimlerChrysler Aerospace">DaimlerChrysler Aerospace</a> (DASA) were said to be keen to create a transnational aerospace and defence company.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The two companies envisaged including A\xc3\xa9rospatiale, the other major European aerospace company, but only after its privatisation.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The first stage of this integration was seen as the transformation of Airbus from a consortium of British Aerospace, DASA, A\xc3\xa9rospatiale and <a href="/wiki/Construcciones_Aeron%C3%A1uticas" class="mw-redirect" title="Construcciones Aeron\xc3\xa1uticas">Construcciones Aeron\xc3\xa1uticas SA</a> into an integrated company; in this aim British Aerospace and DASA were united against the various objections of A\xc3\xa9rospatiale.<sup id="cite_ref-BAeDASArelations_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BAeDASArelations-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> As well as Airbus, British Aerospace and DASA were partners in the <a href="/wiki/Panavia_Tornado" title="Panavia Tornado">Panavia Tornado</a> and Eurofighter Typhoon aircraft projects. Merger discussions began between British Aerospace and DASA in July 1998, just as French participation became more likely with the announcement that A\xc3\xa9rospatiale was to merge with <a href="/wiki/Matra" title="Matra">Matra</a> and emerge with a diluted French government shareholding.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> A merger was agreed between British Aerospace chairman <a href="/wiki/Richard_Evans_(businessman)" title="Richard Evans (businessman)">Richard Evans</a> and DASA CEO <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_E._Schrempp" title="J\xc3\xbcrgen E. Schrempp">J\xc3\xbcrgen Schrempp</a> in December 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-ftBAeDASA_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ftBAeDASA-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Meanwhile, GEC was also under pressure to participate in defence industry consolidation. Reporting the appointment of George Simpson as GEC managing director in 1996, <i>The Independent</i> had said "some analysts believe that Mr Simpson\'s inside knowledge of BAe, a long-rumoured GEC bid target, was a key to his appointment. GEC favours forging a national \'champion\' defence group with BAe to compete with the giant US organisations."<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> When GEC put MES up for sale on 22 December 1998, British Aerospace abandoned the DASA merger in favour of purchasing its British rival. The merger of British Aerospace and MES was announced on 19 January 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Evans stated that in 2004 that his fear was that an American defence contractor would acquire MES and challenge both British Aerospace and DASA.<sup id="cite_ref-ftBAeDASA_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ftBAeDASA-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The merger created a <a href="/wiki/Vertically_integrated" class="mw-redirect" title="Vertically integrated">vertically integrated</a> company which <i>The Scotsman</i> described as "[a combination of British Aerospace\'s] contracting and platform-building skills with Marconi\'s coveted electronics systems capability",<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> for example combining the manufacturer of the Eurofighter with the company that provided many of the aircraft\'s electronic systems; British Aerospace was MES\' largest customer.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> In contrast, DASA\'s response to the breakdown of the merger discussion was to merge with <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9rospatiale" title="A\xc3\xa9rospatiale">A\xc3\xa9rospatiale</a> to create the European Aeronautic Defence and Space Company (<a href="/wiki/EADS" class="mw-redirect" title="EADS">EADS</a>), a <a href="/wiki/Horizontal_integration" title="Horizontal integration">horizontal integration</a>. EADS has since considered a merger with <a href="/wiki/Thales_Group" title="Thales Group">Thales</a> to create a "fully rounded" company.<sup id="cite_ref-integrated_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-integrated-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Seventeen undertakings were given by BAE Systems to the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Trade_and_Industry_(United_Kingdom)" title="Department of Trade and Industry (United Kingdom)">Department of Trade and Industry</a> which prevented a reference of the merger to the <a href="/wiki/Monopolies_and_Mergers_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="Monopolies and Mergers Commission">Monopolies and Mergers Commission</a>. These were largely to ensure that the integrated company would tender sub-contracts to external companies on an equal basis with its subsidiaries. Another condition was the "<a href="/wiki/Chinese_wall" title="Chinese wall">firewalling</a>" of former British Aerospace and MES teams on defence projects such as the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Strike_Fighter_Program" class="mw-redirect" title="Joint Strike Fighter Program">Joint Strike Fighter</a> (JSF). In 2007 the government, on advice from the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Fair_Trading" title="Office of Fair Trading">Office of Fair Trading</a>, announced it had agreed to release BAE Systems from ten of the undertakings due to "a change in circumstances".<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>BAE Systems inherited the UK government owned "golden" share that was established when British Aerospace was privatised. This unique share prevents amendments of certain parts of the company\'s <a href="/wiki/Articles_of_Association_(law)" class="mw-redirect" title="Articles of Association (law)">Articles of Association</a> without the permission of the Secretary of State.<sup id="cite_ref-compcomm_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-compcomm-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> These Articles require that no foreign person or persons acting together may hold more than 15% of the company\'s shares.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>British Aerospace\'s head office was in Warwick House, Farnborough Aerospace Centre in <a href="/wiki/Farnborough,_Hampshire" title="Farnborough, Hampshire">Farnborough, Hampshire</a>. BAE Systems retains this but the <a href="/wiki/Registered_office" title="Registered office">registered office</a>, and base for the senior leadership team, is in the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Westminster" title="City of Westminster">City of Westminster</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000s">2000s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2000s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>BAE Systems\' first annual report identified Airbus, support services to militaries and integrated systems for air, land and naval applications as key areas of growth. It also stated the company\'s desire to both expand in the US and participate in further consolidation in Europe. BAE Systems described 2001 as an "important year" for its European joint ventures, which were reorganised considerably. The company has described the rationale for expansion in the US; "[it] is by far the largest defence market with spend running close to twice that of the Western European nations combined. Importantly, US investment in research and development is significantly higher than in Western Europe."<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/Dick_Olver" title="Dick Olver">Dick Olver</a> was appointed chairman in July 2004 he ordered a review of the company\'s businesses which ruled out further European acquisitions or joint ventures and confirmed a "strategic bias" for expansion and investment in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The review also confirmed the attractiveness of the land systems sector and, with two acquisitions in 2004 and 2005, BAE moved from a limited land systems supplier to the second largest such company in the world. This shift in strategy was described as "remarkable" by the <i>Financial Times</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-baelandshift_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-baelandshift-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Between 2008 and early 2011 BAE acquired five cyber security companies in a shift in strategy to take account of reduced spending by governments on "traditional defence items such as warships and tanks".<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2000 <a href="/wiki/Matra_Marconi_Space" title="Matra Marconi Space">Matra Marconi Space</a>, a joint BAE Systems/Matra company, was merged with the space division of DASA to form <a href="/wiki/Astrium" title="Astrium">Astrium</a>. On 16 June 2003 BAE sold its 25% share to EADS for \xc2\xa384&#160;million, however due to the lossmaking status of the company, BAE Systems invested an equal amount for "restructuring".<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> In January 2001 Airbus Industrie was transformed from an inherently inefficient consortium structure to a formal joint stock company.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-awst_formation_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-awst_formation-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> BAE Systems sold its 54% majority share of <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Canada" class="mw-redirect" title="BAE Systems Canada">BAE Systems Canada</a>, an electronics company, in April for CA$310 (approx. \xc2\xa3197&#160;million as of December 2010).<sup id="cite_ref-acquisitondisposal_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-acquisitondisposal-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> In November 2001, the company announced the closure of the Avro Regional Jet (<a href="/wiki/BAe_146" class="mw-redirect" title="BAe 146">Avro RJ</a>) production line at <a href="/wiki/Woodford,_Cheshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Woodford, Cheshire">Woodford</a> and the cancellation of the Avro RJX, an advanced series of the aircraft family, as the business was "no longer viable".<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The final Avro RJ to be completed became the last British civil airliner. In November 2001 BAE sold its 49.9% share of <a href="/wiki/Thomson_Marconi_Sonar" title="Thomson Marconi Sonar">Thomson Marconi Sonar</a> to Thales for \xc2\xa385&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-acquisitondisposal_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-acquisitondisposal-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> A further step of European defence consolidation was the merger of BAE\'s share of <a href="/wiki/Matra_BAe_Dynamics" title="Matra BAe Dynamics">Matra BAe Dynamics</a> and the missile division of Alenia Marconi Systems (AMS) into <a href="/wiki/MBDA" title="MBDA">MBDA</a> in December. MBDA thus became the world\'s second largest missile manufacturer.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Although EADS has been reported to be interested in acquiring full control of MBDA, BAE has said that, unlike Airbus, MBDA is a "core business".<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Astute1cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Astute1cropped.jpg/170px-Astute1cropped.jpg" width="170" height="242" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Astute1cropped.jpg/255px-Astute1cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Astute1cropped.jpg/340px-Astute1cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="552" data-file-height="785" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Astute1cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Astute-class_submarine" title="Astute-class submarine"><i>Astute</i>-class</a> <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarine</a> project caused BAE to issue a profit warning in 2002 and invest \xc2\xa3250&#160;million to overcome its difficulties.</div></div></div>\n<p>In June 2002, BAE Systems confirmed it was in takeover discussions with <a href="/wiki/TRW_Inc." title="TRW Inc.">TRW</a>, an American aerospace, automotive and defence business. This was prompted by <a href="/wiki/Northrop_Grumman" title="Northrop Grumman">Northrop Grumman</a>\'s \xc2\xa34.1&#160;billion (approx. US$6&#160;billion c. 2002) hostile bid for TRW in February 2002. A bidding war between BAE Systems, Northrop and <a href="/wiki/General_Dynamics" title="General Dynamics">General Dynamics</a> ended on 1 June when Northrop\'s increased bid of \xc2\xa35.1&#160;billion was accepted. On 11 December 2002, the company issued a shock profit warning due to cost overruns of the <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Nimrod_MRA4" title="BAE Systems Nimrod MRA4">Nimrod MRA4</a> maritime reconnaissance/attack aircraft and the <a href="/wiki/Astute-class_submarine" title="Astute-class submarine"><i>Astute</i>-class</a> <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarine</a> projects.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> On 19 February 2003 BAE took a charge of \xc2\xa3750&#160;million against these projects and the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">Ministry of Defence</a> (MOD) agreed to pay a further \xc2\xa3700&#160;million of the cost.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> In 2000 the company had taken a \xc2\xa3300&#160;million "loss charge" on the Nimrod contract which was expected to cover "all the costs of completion of the current contract".<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The UK government, following a cabinet row described as "one of the most bitter Cabinet disputes over defence contracts since the <a href="/wiki/Westland_affair" title="Westland affair">Westland helicopter affair</a> in 1985", ordered 20 <a href="/wiki/BAE_Hawk" class="mw-redirect" title="BAE Hawk">BAE Hawk</a> trainer aircraft with 24 options in July 2003 in a deal worth \xc2\xa3800&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-hawk03_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hawk03-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The deal was significant because it was a factor in India\'s decision to finalise a \xc2\xa31&#160;billion order for 66 Hawks in March 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-hawk03_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hawk03-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Also in July 2003 BAE Systems and <a href="/wiki/Finmeccanica" class="mw-redirect" title="Finmeccanica">Finmeccanica</a> announced their intention to set up three joint venture companies, to be collectively known as <a href="/wiki/Eurosystems" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurosystems">Eurosystems</a>. These companies would have pooled the avionics, <a href="/wiki/C4ISTAR" class="mw-redirect" title="C4ISTAR">C4ISTAR</a> and communications businesses of the two companies.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> However the difficulties of integrating the companies in this way led to a re-evaluation of the proposal; BAE Systems\' 2004 Annual Report states that "recognising the complexity of the earlier proposed Eurosystems transaction with Finmeccanica we have moved to a simpler model". The main part of this deal was the dissolution of AMS and the establishment of <a href="/wiki/SELEX_Sensors_and_Airborne_Systems" class="mw-redirect" title="SELEX Sensors and Airborne Systems">SELEX Sensors and Airborne Systems</a>; BAE Systems sold its 25% share of the latter to Finmeccanica for \xe2\x82\xac400&#160;million (approx. \xc2\xa3270&#160;million c. 2007) in March 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2004, it was reported that the company was considering selling its shipbuilding divisions, <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Naval_Ships" class="mw-redirect" title="BAE Systems Naval Ships">BAE Systems Naval Ships</a> and <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Submarines" class="mw-redirect" title="BAE Systems Submarines">BAE Systems Submarines</a>. It was understood that General Dynamics wished to acquire the submarine building facilities at <a href="/wiki/Barrow-in-Furness" title="Barrow-in-Furness">Barrow-in-Furness</a>, while <a href="/wiki/VT_Group" title="VT Group">VT Group</a> was said to be interested in the remaining yards on the <a href="/wiki/River_Clyde" title="River Clyde">Clyde</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mergerships_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mergerships-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Instead, in 2008 BAE Systems merged its Surface Fleet arm with the shipbuilding operations of VT Group to form <a href="/wiki/BVT_Surface_Fleet" class="mw-redirect" title="BVT Surface Fleet">BVT Surface Fleet</a>, an aim central to the British Government\'s <a href="/wiki/Defence_Industrial_Strategy" title="Defence Industrial Strategy">Defence Industrial Strategy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1BFV01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/1BFV01.jpg/220px-1BFV01.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/1BFV01.jpg/330px-1BFV01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/1BFV01.jpg/440px-1BFV01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="990" data-file-height="649" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1BFV01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>BAE\'s \xc2\xa32.5&#160;billion purchase of United Defense in 2005 added the <a href="/wiki/M2_Bradley" title="M2 Bradley">M2/M3 Bradley</a> family of armoured vehicles to its product line.</div></div></div>\n<p>On 4 June 2004, BAE Systems outbid General Dynamics for <a href="/wiki/Alvis_Vickers" class="mw-redirect" title="Alvis Vickers">Alvis Vickers</a>, the UK\'s main manufacturer of armoured vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Alvis Vickers was merged with the company\'s <a href="/wiki/RO_Defence" class="mw-redirect" title="RO Defence">RO Defence</a> unit to form BAE Systems Land Systems. Recognising the lack of scale of this business compared to General Dynamics, BAE Systems executives soon identified the US defence company <a href="/wiki/United_Defense" title="United Defense">United Defense Industries</a> (UDI), a major competitor to General Dynamics, as a main acquisition target.<sup id="cite_ref-baelandshift_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-baelandshift-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> On 7 March 2005 BAE announced the \xc2\xa32.25&#160;billion (approx. US$4.2&#160;billion c. 2005) acquisition of UDI.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> UDI, now <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Land_and_Armaments" class="mw-redirect" title="BAE Systems Land and Armaments">BAE Systems Land and Armaments</a>, manufactures combat vehicles, artillery systems, naval guns, missile launchers and precision guided munitions.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2005, BAE Systems announced the sale of its German naval systems subsidiary, Atlas Elektronik, to <a href="/wiki/ThyssenKrupp" title="ThyssenKrupp">ThyssenKrupp</a> and EADS. The sale was complicated by the requirement of the German government to approve any sale. The <i>Financial Times</i> described the sale as "cut price" because French company Thales bid \xe2\x82\xac300&#160;million, but was blocked from purchasing Atlas on national security grounds.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> On 31 January 2006 the company announced the sale of BAE Systems Aerostructures to <a href="/wiki/Spirit_AeroSystems,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Spirit AeroSystems, Inc.">Spirit AeroSystems, Inc</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> having said as early as 2002 that it wished to dispose of what it did not regard as a "core business".<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 18 August 2006 Saudi Arabia signed a contract worth \xc2\xa36&#160;billion to \xc2\xa310&#160;billion for 72 Eurofighter Typhoons, to be delivered by BAE Systems.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> On 10 September 2006 the company was awarded a \xc2\xa32.5&#160;billion contract for the upgrade of 80 <a href="/wiki/Royal_Saudi_Air_Force" title="Royal Saudi Air Force">Royal Saudi Air Force</a> Tornado IDSs.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> One of BAE Systems\' major aims, as highlighted in the 2005 Annual Report, was the granting of increased technology transfer between the UK and the US. The F-35 (JSF) programme became the focus of this effort, with British government ministers such as <a href="/wiki/Paul_Drayson,_Baron_Drayson" title="Paul Drayson, Baron Drayson">Lord Drayson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Defence_Procurement_Agency" title="Defence Procurement Agency">Minister for Defence Procurement</a>, suggesting the UK would withdraw from the project without the transfer of technology that would allow the UK to operate and maintain F-35s independently. On 12 December 2006, Lord Drayson signed an agreement which allows "an unbroken British chain of command" for operation of the aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> On 22 December 2006 BAE received a \xc2\xa3947&#160;million contract to provide guaranteed availability of <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> (RAF) Tornados.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 7 May 2007 the company announced its subsidiary BAE Systems Inc. was to purchase <a href="/wiki/Armor_Holdings" title="Armor Holdings">Armor Holdings</a> for \xc2\xa32.3&#160;billion (approx. US$4.5&#160;billion c. 2007) and completed the deal on 31 July 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-Armor_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Armor-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The company is a manufacturer of tactical wheeled vehicles and a provider of vehicle and individual armour systems and survivability technologies.<sup id="cite_ref-Armor_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Armor-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> BAE Systems (and British Aerospace previously) was a technology partner to the <a href="/wiki/McLaren_(racing)" class="mw-redirect" title="McLaren (racing)">McLaren</a> Formula One team from 1996 to December 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-mclarenpr_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mclarenpr-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The partnership originally focused on McLaren\'s F1 car\'s aerodynamics, eventually moving on to carbon fibre techniques, wireless systems and fuel management. BAE Systems\' main interest in the partnership was to learn about the high speed build and operations processes of McLaren.<sup id="cite_ref-mclarenpr_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mclarenpr-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The company announced the acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Tenix_Defence" title="Tenix Defence">Tenix Defence</a>, a major Australian defence contractor on 18 January 2008. The purchase was completed on 27 June for A$775&#160;million (\xc2\xa3373&#160;million) making <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Australia" title="BAE Systems Australia">BAE Systems Australia</a> that country\'s largest defence contractor.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The UK Ministry of Defence awarded BAE Systems a 15-year munitions contract in August 2008 worth up to \xc2\xa33&#160;billion, and known as MASS. The contract guarantees supply of 80% of the UK Armed Forces\' ammunition and required BAE to modernise its munitions manufacturing facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> BAE Systems expanded its intelligence and security business with the \xc2\xa3531&#160;million purchase of <a href="/wiki/Detica" class="mw-redirect" title="Detica">Detica Group</a> in July 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> It continued this strategy with purchases of Danish cyber and intelligence company ETI for approximately $210&#160;million in December 2010, and <a href="/wiki/Norkom" title="Norkom">Norkom Group PLC</a> the following month for \xe2\x82\xac217&#160;million. The latter provides counter fraud and anti-money laundering solutions to the global financial services industry where its software assists institutions to comply with regulations on financial intelligence and monitoring.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Airbus_shareholding">Airbus shareholding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Airbus shareholding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a></div>\n<p>BAE Systems inherited British Aerospace\'s share of Airbus Industrie, which consisted of two factories at <a href="/wiki/Broughton,_Flintshire" title="Broughton, Flintshire">Broughton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Filton" title="Filton">Filton</a>. These facilities manufactured wings for the Airbus family of aircraft. In 2001 Airbus was incorporated as Airbus SAS, a <a href="/wiki/Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_par_actions_simplifi%C3%A9e" title="Soci\xc3\xa9t\xc3\xa9 par actions simplifi\xc3\xa9e">joint stock company</a>. In return for a 20% share in the new company BAE Systems transferred ownership of its Airbus plants (known as <a href="/wiki/Airbus_UK" title="Airbus UK">Airbus UK</a>) to the new company.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Despite repeated suggestions as early as 2000 that BAE Systems wished to sell its 20% share of Airbus, the possibility was denied by the company<sup id="cite_ref-scotsman2000_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scotsman2000-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> until on 6 April 2006 BBC News reported that it was indeed to sell its stake, then "conservatively valued" at \xc2\xa32.4&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Airbus_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Airbus-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Due to the slow pace of informal negotiations, BAE Systems exercised its <a href="/wiki/Put_option" title="Put option">put option</a> which saw investment bank <a href="/wiki/N_M_Rothschild_%26_Sons" title="N M Rothschild &amp; Sons">Rothschild</a> appointed to give an independent valuation. Six days after this process began, Airbus announced delays to the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">A380</a> with significant effects on the value of Airbus shares. On 2 June 2006 Rothschild valued the company\'s share at \xc2\xa31.87&#160;billion, well below its own analysts\' and even EADS\' expectations.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The BAE Systems board recommended that the company proceed with the sale. On 4 October 2006 shareholders voted in favour and the sale was completed on 13 October.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> BAE Systems\' sale of its Airbus share saw the end of UK owned involvement in civil airliner production. Airbus Operations Ltd (the former Airbus UK) continues to be the Airbus "Centre of Excellence" for wing production, employing over 9,500, but is entirely owned by the Airbus Group (formerly EADS).<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010s">2010s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2010s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In February 2010 BAE Systems announced a \xc2\xa3592&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Writedown" class="mw-redirect" title="Writedown">writedown</a> of the former Armor Holdings business following the loss of the <a href="/wiki/Family_of_Medium_Tactical_Vehicles" title="Family of Medium Tactical Vehicles">Family of Medium Tactical Vehicles</a> contract in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> It was outbid by <a href="/wiki/Oshkosh_Corporation" title="Oshkosh Corporation">Oshkosh Corporation</a> for the \xc2\xa32.3&#160;billion ($3.7&#160;billion) contract.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Land and Armaments had been the "star performer" of BAE Systems\' subsidiaries, growing from sales of \xc2\xa3482&#160;million in 2004 to \xc2\xa36.7&#160;billion in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-prelim09_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prelim09-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-findata_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-findata-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>BAE Systems inherited British Aerospace\'s 35% share of <a href="/wiki/Saab_AB" class="mw-redirect" title="Saab AB">Saab AB</a>, with which it produced and marketed the <a href="/wiki/JAS_39_Gripen" class="mw-redirect" title="JAS 39 Gripen">Gripen</a> fighter aircraft. In 2005 it reduced this share to 20.5% and in March 2010 announced its intention to sell the remainder. <i>The Times</i> stated that the decision brought "to an end its controversial relationship with the Gripen fighter aircraft".<sup id="cite_ref-saabsale_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-saabsale-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Several of the export campaigns for the aircraft were subject to allegations of bribery and corruption.<sup id="cite_ref-saabsale_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-saabsale-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Meanwhile, the company was increasing its presence in India with the formation of Defence Land Systems India in April, a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Mahindra_%26_Mahindra" title="Mahindra &amp; Mahindra">Mahindra &amp; Mahindra</a>. BAE Systems holds just 26% of the equity due to Indian foreign direct investment regulations.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The company continued its move into support services in May 2010 with the purchase of the marine support company <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Marine" title="Atlantic Marine">Atlantic Marine</a> for $352&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-us2010_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-us2010-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> In September 2010 BAE Systems announced plans to sell the <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Platform_Solutions" class="mw-redirect" title="BAE Systems Platform Solutions">Platform Solutions</a> division of BAE Systems Inc., which the <i>Financial Times</i> said could yield as much as \xc2\xa31.3&#160;billion. Despite "considerable expressions of interest", the sale was abandoned in January 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-us2010_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-us2010-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-platformdisposal_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-platformdisposal-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> On 19 October 2010 the British government cancelled the <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Nimrod_MRA4" title="BAE Systems Nimrod MRA4">Nimrod project</a> as part of its <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Defence_and_Security_Review_2010" title="Strategic Defence and Security Review 2010">Strategic Defence and Security Review</a>. The purchases of <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Queen Elizabeth-class aircraft carrier"><i>Queen Elizabeth</i>-class</a> <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carriers</a>, the <i>Astute</i>-class submarines, and the <a href="/wiki/Type_26_frigate" title="Type 26 frigate">Type 26 frigates</a> were all confirmed. A new generation of nuclear missile submarines will be built, however the final decision will be delayed until after the next election.<sup id="cite_ref-sdsr_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sdsr-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>BAE Systems sold the regional aircraft lease portfolio and asset management arm of its <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Regional_Aircraft" title="BAE Systems Regional Aircraft">BAE Systems Regional Aircraft</a> business in May 2011. This unit leases the <a href="/wiki/BAe_146" class="mw-redirect" title="BAe 146">BAe 146</a>/Avro RJ family, <a href="/wiki/BAe_ATP" class="mw-redirect" title="BAe ATP">BAe ATP</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Aerospace_Jetstream" title="British Aerospace Jetstream">Jetstream</a> and <a href="/wiki/BAe_748" class="mw-redirect" title="BAe 748">BAe 748</a>. The company retained the support and engineering activities of the business as part of the transaction.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2011, BAE Systems began consultation with unions and workers over plans to cut nearly 3,000 jobs, mostly in the company\'s military aircraft division.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In its 2012 half-year report, the company revealed a 10% decline in revenue in the six months up to 30 June due to falling demand for armaments.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> In May 2012 the governments of the UK and Saudi Arabia reached an agreement on an arms package which saw a \xc2\xa31.6&#160;billion contract awarded to BAE for the delivery of 55 Pilatus PC-21 and 22 BAE Systems Hawk aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> The Sultanate of Oman ordered Typhoon and Hawk aircraft worth \xc2\xa32.5&#160;billion in December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 13 September 2012, it was reported that BAE Systems and <a href="/wiki/EADS" class="mw-redirect" title="EADS">EADS</a> had entered possible merger talks. In case of a potential tie-up, BAE shareholders would own 40% and EADS shareholders would own 60% of the new organisation.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC092012-_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC092012--97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg092012_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg092012-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> On 10 October 2012, the companies said the merger talks had been called off.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2014 it announced the acquisition of US intelligence capability, Signal Innovations Group Inc., to augment imagery and data analysis technologies in its Intelligence &amp; Security business.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2014, BAE was awarded a \xc2\xa3248&#160;million contract from the <a href="/wiki/British_government" class="mw-redirect" title="British government">British government</a> to build three new <a href="/wiki/Offshore_patrol_vessel" class="mw-redirect" title="Offshore patrol vessel">offshore patrol vessels</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2014, BAE Systems and <a href="/wiki/Babcock_International" title="Babcock International">Babcock International</a> won contracts from the British <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">Ministry of Defence</a> worth a total of \xc2\xa33.2&#160;billion to maintain British warships, submarines and naval bases for the following five years.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 9 October 2014, the company announced the loss of 440 management jobs across the country, with 286 of the job cuts in Lancashire. BAE said that the changes are to "make a more efficient and effective business".<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> During 2014 BAE Systems acquired US-based <a href="/wiki/Cybersecurity" class="mw-redirect" title="Cybersecurity">cybersecurity</a> firm Silversky for $232.5&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a>\'s visit to Turkey in January 2017, BAE and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Aerospace_Industries" title="Turkish Aerospace Industries">TAI</a> officials signed an agreement, worth about \xc2\xa3100 million, for BAE to provide assistance in developing the <a href="/wiki/TAI_TFX" class="mw-redirect" title="TAI TFX">TAI TFX</a> aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> On 10 October 2017 BAE announced that it would sack nearly 2,000 out of its approximately 35,000 employees in Britain, mainly due to an order shortage for the <a href="/wiki/Eurofighter_Typhoon" title="Eurofighter Typhoon">Eurofighter Typhoon</a> jet.<sup id="cite_ref-veconomist_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-veconomist-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Products">Products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Products">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Navy_Type_45_Destroyer_HMS_Daring_MOD_45153705.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Royal_Navy_Type_45_Destroyer_HMS_Daring_MOD_45153705.jpg/220px-Royal_Navy_Type_45_Destroyer_HMS_Daring_MOD_45153705.jpg" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Royal_Navy_Type_45_Destroyer_HMS_Daring_MOD_45153705.jpg/330px-Royal_Navy_Type_45_Destroyer_HMS_Daring_MOD_45153705.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Royal_Navy_Type_45_Destroyer_HMS_Daring_MOD_45153705.jpg/440px-Royal_Navy_Type_45_Destroyer_HMS_Daring_MOD_45153705.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2473" data-file-height="1979" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Navy_Type_45_Destroyer_HMS_Daring_MOD_45153705.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Maritime_-_Naval_Ships" class="mw-redirect" title="BAE Systems Maritime - Naval Ships">BAE Systems Maritime - Naval Ships</a> builds the <a href="/wiki/Type_45_destroyer" title="Type 45 destroyer">Type 45 destroyer</a>. Other subsidiaries of BAE supply the <a href="/wiki/4.5_inch_Mark_8_naval_gun" title="4.5 inch Mark 8 naval gun">naval gun</a> and <a href="/wiki/SAMPSON" title="SAMPSON">SAMPSON</a> and <a href="/wiki/S1850M" title="S1850M">S1850M</a> radars for the class</div></div></div>\n<p>BAE Systems plays a significant role in the production of military equipment. In 2008, 95% of BAE Systems\' total sales were military related.<sup id="cite_ref-SIPRItable_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SIPRItable-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It plays important roles in military aircraft production. The company\'s <a href="/wiki/Eurofighter_Typhoon" title="Eurofighter Typhoon">Typhoon</a> fighter and <a href="/wiki/Panavia_Tornado" title="Panavia Tornado">Tornado</a> fighter-bomber are both front line aircraft of the RAF.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> The company is a major partner in the F-35 Lightning II programme.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/BAE_Hawk" class="mw-redirect" title="BAE Hawk">Hawk</a> advanced jet trainer aircraft has been widely exported.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> In July 2006, the British government declassified the <a href="/wiki/BAE_HERTI" class="mw-redirect" title="BAE HERTI">HERTI</a> (High Endurance Rapid Technology Insertion), an <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_Aerial_Vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Unmanned Aerial Vehicle">Unmanned Aerial Vehicle</a> (UAV) which can navigate autonomously.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> It is currently developing a <a href="/wiki/Sixth-generation_jet_fighter" title="Sixth-generation jet fighter">sixth-generation jet fighter</a> aircraft for the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">RAF</a> marketed as the "<a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Tempest" title="BAE Systems Tempest">Tempest</a>". It is being developed by "Team Tempest" consisting of, UK <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">Ministry of Defence</a>, BAE Systems, <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Holdings" title="Rolls-Royce Holdings">Rolls-Royce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_S.p.A." title="Leonardo S.p.A.">Leonardo S.p.A.</a> and <a href="/wiki/MBDA" title="MBDA">MBDA</a>, and is intended to enter service from 2035 replacing the <a href="/wiki/Eurofighter_Typhoon" title="Eurofighter Typhoon">Eurofighter Typhoon</a> aircraft in service with the RAF.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Land_and_Armaments" class="mw-redirect" title="BAE Systems Land and Armaments">BAE Systems Land and Armaments</a> manufactures the <a href="/wiki/M2_Bradley" title="M2 Bradley">M2/M3 Bradley</a> fighting vehicle family, the US Navy <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Gun_System" title="Advanced Gun System">Advanced Gun System</a> (AGS), <a href="/wiki/M113_armoured_personnel_carrier" class="mw-redirect" title="M113 armoured personnel carrier">M113</a> armoured personnel carrier (APC), <a href="/wiki/M109_howitzer" title="M109 howitzer">M109 Paladin</a>, <a href="/wiki/M777_howitzer" title="M777 howitzer">M777 howitzer</a>, the British Army\'s <a href="/wiki/Challenger_2_tank" class="mw-redirect" title="Challenger 2 tank">Challenger II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warrior_Tracked_Armoured_Vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Warrior Tracked Armoured Vehicle">Warrior Tracked Armoured Vehicle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panther_Command_and_Liaison_Vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Panther Command and Liaison Vehicle">Panther Command and Liaison Vehicle</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/SA80" title="SA80">SA80</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Major naval projects include the <a href="/wiki/Astute-class_submarine" title="Astute-class submarine"><i>Astute</i>-class</a> nuclear submarine, <a href="/wiki/Type_45_destroyer" title="Type 45 destroyer">Type 45</a> air defence destroyer and <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Queen Elizabeth-class aircraft carrier"><i>Queen Elizabeth</i>-class</a> aircraft carrier.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Areas_of_business">Areas of business</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Areas of business">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>BAE Systems defines its "home markets" to be Australia, India, Saudi Arabia, the UK and the US.<sup id="cite_ref-about_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>BAE Systems is the predominant supplier to the UK <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">Ministry of Defence</a> (MoD); in 2009/2010 BAE Systems companies in the list of Top 100 suppliers to the MoD received contracts totalling \xc2\xa33.98&#160;billion, with total revenue being higher when other subsidiary income is included.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> In comparison, the second largest supplier is <a href="/wiki/Babcock_International_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Babcock International Group">Babcock International Group</a> and its subsidiaries, with a revenue of \xc2\xa31.1&#160;billion from the MoD. Oxford Economic Forecasting states that in 2002 the company\'s UK businesses employed 111,578 people, achieved export sales of \xc2\xa33&#160;billion and paid \xc2\xa32.6&#160;billion in taxes. These figures exclude the contribution of Airbus UK.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After its creation, BAE Systems had a difficult relationship with the MoD. This was attributed to deficient project management by the company, but also in part to the deficiencies in the terms of "fixed price contracts". CEO <a href="/wiki/Michael_Turner_(businessman)" title="Michael Turner (businessman)">Mike Turner</a> said in 2006 "We had entered into contracts under the old competition rules that frankly we shouldn\'t have taken".<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> These competition rules were introduced by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Levene,_Baron_Levene_of_Portsoken" title="Peter Levene, Baron Levene of Portsoken">Lord Levene</a> during the 1980s to shift the burden of risk to the contractor and were in contrast to "cost plus contracts" where a contractor was paid for the value of its product plus an agreed profit.<sup id="cite_ref-basic_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-basic-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>BAE Systems was operating in "the only truly open defence market",<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> which meant that it was competing with US and European companies for British defence projects, while they were protected in their home markets. The US defence market is competitive, however largely between American firms, while foreign companies are excluded. In December 2005 the MoD published the Defence Industrial Strategy (DIS) which has been widely acknowledged to recognise BAE Systems as the UK\'s "national champion".<sup id="cite_ref-econdis_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econdis-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> The DIS identifies key industrial capabilities which must be maintained within the UK through long-term government commitments to support research spending and procurement. Of these capabilities, several are dominated by BAE Systems, including naval vessels and submarines, combat vehicles, fixed-wing aircraft, general munitions (with the exception of certain "niche capabilities abroad") and <a href="/wiki/Network-enabled_capability" title="Network-enabled capability">network-enabled capability</a> (defined as C4ISTAR in the DIS). The company maintains an interest in future UAV technologies through its collaborative FLAVIIR research programme with <a href="/wiki/Engineering_and_Physical_Sciences_Research_Council" title="Engineering and Physical Sciences Research Council">EPSRC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the publication of the DIS BAE Systems CEO Mike Turner said "If we didn\'t have the DIS and our profitability and the terms of trade had stayed as they were... then there had to be a question mark about our future in the UK".<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Lord Levene said in the balance between value for money or maintaining a viable industrial base the DIS "tries as well as it can to steer a middle course and to achieve as much as it can in both directions. ...We will never have a perfect solution."<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2012, the MOD awarded BAE Systems a \xc2\xa3328m contract to design the UK\'s next generation nuclear-armed submarines.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 6 November 2013, BAE Systems announced that 1,775 jobs are to go at its yards in England and Scotland. Shipbuilding will cease entirely in Portsmouth in 2014 with the loss of 940 jobs, and a further 835 jobs would be lost at Filton, near Bristol, and at the shipyards in Govan, Rosyth, and Scotstoun in Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Inc." title="BAE Systems Inc.">BAE Systems Inc.</a></div>\n<p>The attraction of MES to British Aerospace was largely its ownership of Tracor, a major American defence contractor.<sup id="cite_ref-integrated_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-integrated-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>BAE Systems Inc. now sells more to the US Department of Defense (DOD) than the UK MoD.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> The company has been allowed to buy important defence contractors in the US, however its status as a UK company requires that its US subsidiaries are governed by American executives under <a href="/wiki/Special_Security_Arrangement" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Security Arrangement">Special Security Arrangements</a>. The company faces fewer impediments in this sense than its European counterparts, as there is a high <a href="/wiki/Special_Relationship_(US-UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Relationship (US-UK)">degree of integration</a> between the US and UK defence establishments. BAE Systems\' purchase of <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin_Aerospace_Electronic_Systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Lockheed Martin Aerospace Electronic Systems">Lockheed Martin Aerospace Electronic Systems</a> in November 2000 was described by <a href="/wiki/John_Hamre" title="John Hamre">John Hamre</a>, CEO of the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Strategic_and_International_Studies" title="Center for Strategic and International Studies">Center for Strategic and International Studies</a> and former <a href="/wiki/United_States_Deputy_Secretary_of_Defense" title="United States Deputy Secretary of Defense">Deputy Secretary of Defense</a>, as "precedent setting" given the advanced and classified nature of many of that company\'s products.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The possibility of a merger between BAE Systems Inc. and major North American defence contractors has long been reported, including Boeing, General Dynamics, Lockheed Martin, and Raytheon.<sup id="cite_ref-mergerships_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mergerships-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rest_of_the_world">Rest of the world</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Rest of the world">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Australia" title="BAE Systems Australia">BAE Systems Australia</a> is one of the largest defence contractors in Australia, having more than doubled in size with the acquisition of Tenix Defence in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> The Al Yamamah agreements between the UK and Saudi Arabia require "the provision of a complete defence package for the Kingdom of Saudi Arabia"; BAE Systems employs 4,600 people in the kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Land_Systems_South_Africa" title="BAE Systems Land Systems South Africa">BAE Systems Land Systems South Africa</a>, 75% owned by BAE Systems, is the largest military vehicle manufacturer in South Africa, and is currently taking part in the US <a href="/wiki/MRAP" title="MRAP">MRAP</a> programme. BAE Systems\' interests in Sweden are a result of the purchases of <a href="/wiki/Alvis_plc" title="Alvis plc">Alvis Vickers</a> and UDI, which owned H\xc3\xa4gglunds and <a href="/wiki/Bofors" title="Bofors">Bofors</a> respectively; the companies are now part of <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_AB" title="BAE Systems AB">BAE Systems AB</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Shareholders">Shareholders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Shareholders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>As of 8 October 2012 BAE Systems listed the following as "significant" shareholders: <a href="/wiki/Invesco_Perpetual" title="Invesco Perpetual">Invesco Perpetual</a> (13.38%), <a href="/wiki/BlackRock" title="BlackRock">BlackRock</a> (4.66%), <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Resources" class="mw-redirect" title="Franklin Resources">Franklin Templeton Investments</a> (3.95%) and <a href="/wiki/Legal_%26_General" title="Legal &amp; General">Legal &amp; General</a> (3.62%).<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organisation">Organisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Organisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FarnboroughAerospaceCentre_panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/68/FarnboroughAerospaceCentre_panorama.jpg/220px-FarnboroughAerospaceCentre_panorama.jpg" width="220" height="91" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/68/FarnboroughAerospaceCentre_panorama.jpg/330px-FarnboroughAerospaceCentre_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/68/FarnboroughAerospaceCentre_panorama.jpg/440px-FarnboroughAerospaceCentre_panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1106" data-file-height="458" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FarnboroughAerospaceCentre_panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>BAE Systems has offices in the Farnborough Aerospace Centre business park. Senior managers are based at the <a href="/wiki/Registered_office" title="Registered office">registered office</a> in <a href="/wiki/1_Carlton_Gardens" class="mw-redirect" title="1 Carlton Gardens">Carlton Gardens</a>, <a href="/wiki/City_of_Westminster" title="City of Westminster">City of Westminster</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:6_Carlton_Gardens,_London,_SW1Y_5AD,_United_Kingdom.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/6_Carlton_Gardens%2C_London%2C_SW1Y_5AD%2C_United_Kingdom.JPG/440px-6_Carlton_Gardens%2C_London%2C_SW1Y_5AD%2C_United_Kingdom.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="4608" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:6_Carlton_Gardens,_London,_SW1Y_5AD,_United_Kingdom.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>6 Carlton Gardens, London</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurofighter_Typhoon_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Eurofighter_Typhoon_2.jpg/220px-Eurofighter_Typhoon_2.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage"
