//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Eurofighter_Typhoon_2.jpg/440px-Eurofighter_Typhoon_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="837" data-file-height="471" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurofighter_Typhoon_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A BAE assembled Eurofighter Typhoon <a href="/wiki/Eurofighter_Typhoon_variants" title="Eurofighter Typhoon variants">T1</a>. BAE is a partner in <a href="/wiki/Eurofighter_GmbH" title="Eurofighter GmbH">Eurofighter GmbH</a>, the multinational company that coordinates the design, production, and upgrade of the aircraft.</div></div></div>\n<p>BAE Systems has its head office and its <a href="/wiki/Registered_office" title="Registered office">registered office</a> in <a href="/wiki/City_of_Westminster" title="City of Westminster">City of Westminster</a>, London.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> In addition to its central London offices, it has an office in <a href="/wiki/Farnborough,_Hampshire" title="Farnborough, Hampshire">Farnborough, Hampshire</a> that houses functional specialists and support functions.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The company divides its business into the following business groups:<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Applied Intelligence</dt>\n<dd>This division delivers hardware and software tools to protect and enhance critical assets. The division includes <a href="/wiki/Detica" class="mw-redirect" title="Detica">BAE Systems Applied Intelligence</a>.</dd>\n<dt>Saudi Arabia</dt>\n<dd>This division supports customers in Saudi Arabia, including the Al Yamamah project and subsequent Saudi Typhoon contract.</dd>\n<dt>Intelligence &amp; Security</dt>\n<dd>This division provides mission-critical cyber security tools, information technology and intelligence and analytical and support tools</dd>\n<dt>Maritime</dt>\n<dd>This division designs and manufactures naval ships and submarines. The division includes <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Maritime_%E2%80%93_Naval_Ships" title="BAE Systems Maritime \xe2\x80\x93 Naval Ships">BAE Systems Maritime \xe2\x80\x93 Naval Ships</a> and <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Maritime_%E2%80%93_Submarines" title="BAE Systems Maritime \xe2\x80\x93 Submarines">BAE Systems Maritime \xe2\x80\x93 Submarines</a>. Maritime has inherited the naval systems businesses of Insyte, for example <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Integrated_System_Technologies" title="BAE Systems Integrated System Technologies">BAE Systems Underwater Systems</a> and naval radar.</dd>\n<dt>Regional Aircraft</dt>\n<dd>This division provides regional aircraft and support services to regional airlines</dd>\n<dt>Australia</dt>\n<dd>This division supports customers in Australia</dd>\n<dt>Electronic Systems</dt>\n<dd>This division supplies flight and engine controls for electronic warfare and night vision systems, surveillance and reconnaissance sensors, secure networked communications equipment, and power and energy management systems</dd>\n<dt>Platforms &amp; Services</dt>\n<dd>This division designs, develops, produces, supports, maintains, modernises and upgrades armoured combat vehicles, wheeled vehicles, naval guns, surface ship combatants, commercial vessels, missile launchers, artillery systems, military ordnance, and protective wear and armour. This division includes <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Land_%26_Armaments" title="BAE Systems Land &amp; Armaments">BAE Systems Land &amp; Armaments</a>. It also includes projects such as <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Taranis" title="BAE Systems Taranis">Taranis</a>. The company\'s 33% share of <a href="/wiki/Eurofighter_GmbH" title="Eurofighter GmbH">Eurofighter Jagdflugzeug GmbH</a> (33%) represents its involvement in the Eurofighter Typhoon project.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup></dd>\n<dt>Military Air &amp; Information</dt>\n<dd>This division provides information superiority and air power to customers. The division includes <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Military_Air_%26_Information" title="BAE Systems Military Air &amp; Information">BAE Systems Military Air &amp; Information</a></dd>\n<dt>Shared Services</dt>\n<dd>This division provides shared capabilities and support services, principally to internal customers. It also includes a 49% interest in <a href="/wiki/Air_Astana" title="Air Astana">Air Astana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_governance">Corporate governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Corporate governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>BAE Systems\' chairman is Sir <a href="/wiki/Roger_Carr_(businessman)" title="Roger Carr (businessman)">Roger Carr</a>. The executive directors are <a href="/wiki/Charles_Woodburn" title="Charles Woodburn">Charles Woodburn</a> (CEO), Peter Lynas, and Jerry DeMuro. The non-executive directors are <a href="/wiki/Harriet_Green" title="Harriet Green">Harriet Green</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Grigg" title="Chris Grigg">Chris Grigg</a>, Nick Rose, Paula Rosput Reynolds, Ian Tyler, and <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Corley" title="Elizabeth Corley">Elizabeth Corley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The company\'s first CEO, John Weston, was forced to resign in 2002 in a boardroom "coup" and was replaced by Mike Turner.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Business</i> reported that Weston was ousted when non-executive directors informed the chairman that they had lost confidence in him. Further, it was suggested that at least one non-executive director was encouraged to make such a move by the MOD due to the increasingly fractious relationship between BAE Systems and the government.<sup id="cite_ref-Business_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Business-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> As well as the terms of the Nimrod contract, Weston had fought against the MOD\'s insistence that one of the first three Type 45 destroyers should be built by VT Group. <i>The Business</i> said he considered this "competition-policy gone mad".<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It is understood that Turner had a poor working relationship with senior MOD officials, (for example with former Defence Secretary <a href="/wiki/Geoff_Hoon" title="Geoff Hoon">Geoff Hoon</a>) Significantly the first meeting between Olver and Hoon was said to have gone well, a MOD official commented "He is a man we can do business with. We think it is good to be taking a fresh look at things."<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> It has been suggested that relations between Turner and Olver were tense.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> On 16 October 2007 the company announced that Mike Turner would retire in August 2008. <i>The Times</i> called his departure plans "abrupt" and a "shock", given previous statements that he wished to retire in 2013 at the age of 65.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> Despite suggestions that BAE Systems would prefer an American CEO due to the increasing importance of the United States defence market to the company and the opportunity to make a clean break from corruption allegations and investigations related to the <a href="/wiki/Al_Yamamah" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Yamamah">Al Yamamah</a> contracts the company announced on 27 June 2008 that it had selected the company\'s chief operating officer, Ian King, to succeed Turner with effect from 1 September 2008; <i>The Financial Times</i> noted that King\'s career at Marconi distances him from the British Aerospace-led Al Yamamah project.<sup id="cite_ref-ftbaesearch_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ftbaesearch-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2015 the company invested more than \xc2\xa311m in charities and not-for-profit organisations through company and employee donations to support its key areas of customer, education and heritage.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 22 February 2017 BAE Systems announced that on that day Ian King had informed the Board that he would retire on 30 June 2017. It was confirmed that Charles Woodburn, currently Chief Operating Officer, will be appointed as Chief Executive from 1 July 2017. Woodburn joined BAE Systems in May 2016 as Chief Operating Officer and Executive Board Director, following over 20 years\' international experience in senior management positions in the oil and gas industry.)<sup id="cite_ref-Ian_King,_Chief_Executive,_BAE_Systems_plc,_has_today_informed_the_Board_that_he_will_retire_on_30_June_2017._151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ian_King,_Chief_Executive,_BAE_Systems_plc,_has_today_informed_the_Board_that_he_will_retire_on_30_June_2017.-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Woodburn is aiming to make BAE more efficient and technologically innovative.<sup id="cite_ref-veconomist_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-veconomist-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_information">Financial information</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Financial information">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Financial information for the Company is as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-prelims_3-5" 2004\n</td>\n<td>13,222\n</td>\n<td>730\n</td>\n<td>3\n</td>\n<td>17.4\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>31 December 2003<sup id="cite_ref-gaap_156-0" class="reference"><a class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gaap-156">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>12,145\n</td>\n<td>(616)\n</td>\n<td>(686)<sup id="cite_ref-nimrod_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nimrod-157">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>17.3\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>31 December 2001<sup id="cite_ref-gaap_156-2" class="reference"><a class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gaap-156">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>12,185\n</td>\n<td>179\n</td>\n<td>(19)\n</td>\n<td>18.8\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>31 December 1999<sup id="cite_ref-gaap_156-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gaap-156">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>8,929\n</td>\n<td>459\n</td>\n<td>328\n</td>\n<td>29.4\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-airbus-155"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-airbus_155-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Restated to exclude Airbus contributions. Included for comparison.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-gaap-156"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-gaap_156-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-gaap_156-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-gaap_156-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-gaap_156-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-gaap_156-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Data prepared using UK <a href="/wiki/Generally_Accepted_Accounting_Principles" class="mw-redirect" title="Generally Accepted Accounting Principles">GAAP</a> guidelines. Standards</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-nimrod-157"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-nimrod_157-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Reflects \xc2\xa3750&#160;million charges for problems with Nimrod MRA4 (\xc2\xa3500&#160;million) and <i>Astute</i>-class submarine (\xc2\xa3250&#160;million) programmes.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Bae_systems_financial_information_1999_-_2017.png" class="image" title="Bae systems financial information 1999 - 2017"><img alt="Bae systems financial information 1999 - 2017" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Bae_systems_financial_information_1999_-_2017.png/800px-Bae_systems_financial_information_1999_-_2017.png" width="800" height="519" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Bae_systems_financial_information_1999_-_2017.png/1200px-Bae_systems_financial_information_1999_-_2017.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Bae_systems_financial_information_1999_-_2017.png/1600px-Bae_systems_financial_information_1999_-_2017.png 2x" data-file-width="3573" data-file-height="2318" /></a></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corruption_investigations">Corruption investigations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Corruption investigations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Serious_Fraud_Office">Serious Fraud Office</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Serious Fraud Office">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>BAE Systems has been under investigation by the <a href="/wiki/Serious_Fraud_Office_(United_Kingdom)" title="Serious Fraud Office (United Kingdom)">Serious Fraud Office</a>, into the use of political corruption to help sell arms to Chile, Czech Republic, Romania, Saudi Arabia, South Africa, Tanzania and Qatar.<sup id="cite_ref-SevenCountries_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SevenCountries-158">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GordonIntervene_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GordonIntervene-159">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-solicitorgeneral_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solicitorgeneral-160">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> In response, BAE Systems\' 2006 Corporate Responsibility Report states "We continue to reject these allegations... We take our obligations under the law extremely seriously and will continue to comply with all legal requirements around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> In June 2007 <a href="/wiki/Lord_Woolf" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Woolf">Lord Woolf</a> was selected to lead what the BBC described as an "independent review.... [an] ethics committee to look into how the defence giant conducts its arms deals."<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> The report, <i>Ethical business conduct in BAE Systems plc \xe2\x80\x93 the way forward</i>, made 23 recommendations, measures which the company has committed to implement. The finding stated that "in the past BAE did not pay sufficient attention to ethical standards in the way it conducted business," and was described by the BBC as "an embarrassing admission."<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2009, the Serious Fraud Office announced that it intended to prosecute BAE Systems for offences relating to overseas corruption. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> claimed that a penalty "possibly of more than" \xc2\xa3500 million might be an acceptable settlement package.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> On 5 February 2010, BAE Systems agreed to pay criminal fines of \xc2\xa3257 million (US$400 million) to the US<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> and \xc2\xa330M to the UK. The UK had already massively benefited from \xc2\xa343&#160;billion contract in tax receipts and jobs in the UK, and dropped an anti-corruption investigation into the <a href="/wiki/Al-Yamamah_arms_deal" title="Al-Yamamah arms deal">Al Yamamah contracts</a> later taken up by US authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> Crucially, under a plea bargain with the <a href="/wiki/US_Department_of_Justice" class="mw-redirect" title="US Department of Justice">US Department of Justice</a>, BAE Systems was convicted of felony conspiracy to defraud the United States government and sentenced in March 2010 by US District Court Judge <a href="/wiki/John_D._Bates" title="John D. Bates">John D. Bates</a> to pay a $400&#160;million fine, one of the largest fines in the history of the DOJ. Judge Bates said the company\'s conduct involved "deception, duplicity and knowing violations of law, I think it\'s fair to say, on an enormous scale".<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> BAE Systems did not directly admit to bribery, and is thus not internationally blacklisted from future contracts. Some of the \xc2\xa330M penalty the company will pay in fines to the UK will be paid ex gratia for the benefit of the people of Tanzania.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> On 2 March 2010 Campaign Against Arms Trade and The Corner House were successful in gaining a High Court injunction on the Serious Fraud Office\'s settlement with BAE Systems. The High Court may order a full review of the settlement.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Saudi_Arabia">Saudi Arabia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Saudi Arabia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Parking_RSAF_Tornado_in_1991.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Parking_RSAF_Tornado_in_1991.jpg/220px-Parking_RSAF_Tornado_in_1991.jpg" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Parking_RSAF_Tornado_in_1991.jpg/330px-Parking_RSAF_Tornado_in_1991.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Parking_RSAF_Tornado_in_1991.jpg/440px-Parking_RSAF_Tornado_in_1991.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1996" data-file-height="1176" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Parking_RSAF_Tornado_in_1991.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>One of 24 <a href="/wiki/Panavia_Tornado_ADV" title="Panavia Tornado ADV">Panavia Tornado ADVs</a> delivered to the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Saudi_Air_Force" title="Royal Saudi Air Force">Royal Saudi Air Force</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Al_Yamamah_arms_sales" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Yamamah arms sales">Al Yamamah arms sales</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Al-Yamamah_arms_deal" title="Al-Yamamah arms deal">Al-Yamamah arms deal</a></div>\n<p>Both BAE Systems and its previous incarnation British Aerospace have long been the subject of allegations of bribery in relation to its business in Saudi Arabia. The UK <a href="/wiki/National_Audit_Office_(United_Kingdom)" title="National Audit Office (United Kingdom)">National Audit Office</a> (NAO) investigated the Al Yamamah contracts and has so far not published its conclusions, the only NAO report ever to be withheld.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> The MOD has stated "The report remains sensitive. Disclosure would harm both international relations and the UK\'s commercial interests."<sup id="cite_ref-SFO_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SFO-173">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> The company has been accused of maintaining a \xc2\xa360&#160;million Saudi <a href="/wiki/Slush_fund" title="Slush fund">slush fund</a> and was the subject of an investigation by the Serious Fraud Office (SFO). On 14 December 2006 it was announced that the SFO was "discontinuing" its investigation into the company. It stated that representations to its Director and the <a href="/wiki/Attorney_General_for_England_and_Wales" title="Attorney General for England and Wales">Attorney General</a> <a href="/wiki/Peter_Goldsmith,_Baron_Goldsmith" title="Peter Goldsmith, Baron Goldsmith">Lord Goldsmith</a> had led to the conclusion that the wider public interest "to safeguard national and international security" outweighed any potential benefits of further investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> The termination of the investigation has been controversial.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> In June 2007, the BBC\'s <a href="/wiki/Panorama_(TV_series)" title="Panorama (TV series)">Panorama</a> alleged BAE Systems "paid hundreds of millions of pounds to the ex-Saudi ambassador to the US, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Bandar_bin_Sultan" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince Bandar bin Sultan">Prince Bandar bin Sultan</a>" in return for his role in the Al Yamamah deals.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> In late June 2007 the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">United States Department of Justice</a> (DOJ) began a formal investigation into BAE\'s compliance with anti-corruption laws.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> On 19 May 2008 BAE Systems confirmed that its CEO Mike Turner and non-executive director <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Rudd" title="Nigel Rudd">Nigel Rudd</a> had been detained "for about 20 minutes" at two US airports the previous week and that the DOJ had issued "a number of additional subpoenas in the US to employees of BAE Systems plc and BAE Systems Inc as part of its ongoing investigation".<sup id="cite_ref-dojdetentions_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dojdetentions-178">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Times</i> suggested that such "humiliating behaviour by the DOJ" is unusual toward a company that is co-operating fully.<sup id="cite_ref-dojdetentions_178-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dojdetentions-178">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A judicial review of the decision by the SFO to drop the investigation was granted on 9 November 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> On 10 April 2008 the High Court ruled that the SFO "acted unlawfully" by dropping its investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Times</i> described the ruling as "one of the most strongly worded judicial attacks on government action" which condemned how "ministers \'buckled\' to \'blatant threats\' that Saudi cooperation in the fight against terror would end unless the ...investigation was dropped."<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> On 24 April the SFO was granted leave to appeal to the House of Lords against the ruling.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> There was a two-day hearing before the Lords on 7 and 8 July 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> On 30 July the House of Lords unanimously overturned the High Court ruling, stating that the decision to discontinue the investigation was lawful.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Others">Others</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Others">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Regele_Ferdinand_Frigate_22.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Regele_Ferdinand_Frigate_22.jpg/150px-Regele_Ferdinand_Frigate_22.jpg" width="150" height="217" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Regele_Ferdinand_Frigate_22.jpg/225px-Regele_Ferdinand_Frigate_22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Regele_Ferdinand_Frigate_22.jpg/300px-Regele_Ferdinand_Frigate_22.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1063" data-file-height="1540" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Regele_Ferdinand_Frigate_22.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/HMS_Coventry_(F98)" title="HMS Coventry (F98)">HMS <i>Coventry</i></a> was one of two frigates sold to Romania.</div></div></div>\n<p>In September 2005 <i>The Guardian</i> reported that banking records showed that BAE Systems paid \xc2\xa31&#160;million to <a href="/wiki/Augusto_Pinochet" title="Augusto Pinochet">Augusto Pinochet</a>, the former Chilean dictator.<sup id="cite_ref-Pinochet_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pinochet-185">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Guardian</i> has also reported that "clandestine arms deals" have been under investigation in Chile and the UK since 2003 and that British Aerospace and BAE Systems made a number of payments to Pinochet advisers.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> In 2003, <a href="/wiki/HMS_Sheffield_(F96)" title="HMS Sheffield (F96)">HMS <i>Sheffield</i></a> was sold to the <a href="/wiki/Chilean_Navy" title="Chilean Navy">Chilean Navy</a> for \xc2\xa327&#160;million, however the government\'s profit from the sale was \xc2\xa33&#160;million, after contracts worth \xc2\xa324&#160;million were placed with BAE Systems for upgrade and refurbishment of the ship.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_292006_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_292006-187">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>BAE Systems is alleged to have paid "secret offshore commissions" of over \xc2\xa37&#160;million to secure the sale of <a href="/wiki/HMS_London_(F95)" title="HMS London (F95)">HMS <i>London</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/HMS_Coventry_(F98)" title="HMS Coventry (F98)">HMS <i>Coventry</i></a> to the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanian Navy">Romanian Navy</a>. The company received a \xc2\xa3116&#160;million contract for the refurbishment of the ships prior to delivery;<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> however the British taxpayer only received the scrap value of \xc2\xa3100,000 each from the sale.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>BAE Systems ran into controversy in 2002 over the abnormally high cost of a radar system sold to <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gdn101219_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gdn101219-191">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> The sale was criticised by several opposition MPs and the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_International_Development" title="Secretary of State for International Development">Secretary of State for International Development</a> <a href="/wiki/Clare_Short" title="Clare Short">Clare Short</a> declared that BAE Systems had "ripped off" developing nations.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> In December 2010, leaked US diplomatic communications revealed that Edward Hoseah, the Tanzanian prosecutor investigating misconduct by BAE Systems, had confided in US diplomats that "his life may be in danger" and was being routinely threatened.<sup id="cite_ref-gdn101219_191-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gdn101219-191">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2007, details of an investigation by the Serious Fraud Office into BAE Systems\' sales tactics in regard to South Africa were reported, highlighting the \xc2\xa32.3&#160;billion deal to supply <a href="/wiki/Hawk_trainers" class="mw-redirect" title="Hawk trainers">Hawk trainers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gripen_fighters" class="mw-redirect" title="Gripen fighters">Gripen fighters</a> as suspect.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> In May 2011, as allegations of bribery behind South Africa\'s Gripen procurement continued, the company\'s partner <a href="/wiki/Saab_AB" class="mw-redirect" title="Saab AB">Saab AB</a> issued strong denials of any illicit payments being made; however in June 2011 Saab announced that BAE Systems had made unaccounted payments of roughly $3.5&#160;million to a consultant, this revelation prompted South African Opposition parties to call for a renewed inquiry.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> The Gripen\'s procurement by the Czech Republic was also under investigation by the Serious Fraud Office in 2006 over allegations of bribery.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_292006_187-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_292006-187">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Espionage">Espionage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Espionage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In September 2003 <i>The Sunday Times</i> reported that BAE Systems had hired a private security contractor to collate information about individuals working at the <a href="/wiki/Campaign_Against_Arms_Trade" title="Campaign Against Arms Trade">Campaign Against Arms Trade</a> and their activities.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> In February 2007, it was reported that the corporation had again obtained private confidential information from CAAT.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The company was reported in 2012 to have been the target of Chinese <a href="/wiki/Cyber_espionage" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyber espionage">cyber espionage</a> that may have stolen secrets related to the <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin_F-35_Lightning_II" title="Lockheed Martin F-35 Lightning II">Lockheed Martin F-35 Lightning II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nuclear_weapons">Nuclear weapons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Nuclear weapons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2006, BAE Systems was excluded from the <a href="/wiki/Portfolio_(finance)" title="Portfolio (finance)">portfolio</a> of the <a href="/wiki/The_Government_Pension_Fund_of_Norway" class="mw-redirect" title="The Government Pension Fund of Norway">government pension fund of Norway</a> "because they develop and/or produce central components for nuclear weapons".<sup id="cite_ref-Norway_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Norway-202">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> "According to the ethical guidelines for the [Norwegian] Government Pension Fund \xe2\x80\x93 Global, companies that produce weapons that through normal use may violate fundamental <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_principles" title="Humanitarian principles">humanitarian principles</a> shall be excluded from the fund."<sup id="cite_ref-Norway_202-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Norway-202">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> BAE Systems is indirectly engaged in production of <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear weapons">nuclear weapons</a> \xe2\x80\x93 through its 37.5% share of <a href="/wiki/MBDA" title="MBDA">MBDA</a> it is involved with the production and support of the <a href="/wiki/Air-Sol_Moyenne_Port%C3%A9e" title="Air-Sol Moyenne Port\xc3\xa9e">ASMP</a> missile, an air-launched nuclear missile which forms part of the <a href="/wiki/Force_de_frappe" class="mw-redirect" title="Force de frappe">French nuclear deterrent</a>. The company is also the UK\'s only <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_submarine" title="Nuclear submarine">nuclear submarine</a> manufacturer and thus produces a key element of the United Kingdom\'s nuclear weapons capability.  However, commentators pointed out Norway has bound their strategic defence to the UK\'s "since Napoleonic times", including both protection under the British nuclear deterrent as well as the joint NATO nuclear sharing policy.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cluster_bombs">Cluster bombs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Cluster bombs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>BAE Systems was in 2003 initially criticised for its role in the production of <a href="/wiki/Cluster_bombs" class="mw-redirect" title="Cluster bombs">cluster bombs</a>, due to the long term risk for injury or death to civilians. Following the 2008 Oslo <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Cluster_Munitions" title="Convention on Cluster Munitions">Convention on Cluster Munitions</a> BAE Systems was among the first defence contractors to stop their manufacture<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> and by 2012 the majority of the munitions had been destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Saudi_war_crimes_in_Yemen">Saudi war crimes in Yemen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Saudi war crimes in Yemen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Saudi Arabia is BAE\'s third biggest market.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Independent</i> reported that "in 2014, British defence firm BAE won a contract worth \xc2\xa34.4bn to supply the Saudis with 72 fighter jets \xe2\x80\x93 some of which were <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen#Reports_of_war_crimes" title="Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen">used to bomb Red Cross and MSF hospitals in Yemen</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> The chairman of BAE Systems, Sir <a href="/wiki/Roger_Carr_(businessman)" title="Roger Carr (businessman)">Roger Carr</a>, rejected criticism over BAE\'s continued work in Saudi Arabia, saying "We will stop doing it when they tell us to stop doing it. ...  We maintain peace by having the ability to make war and that has stood the test of time."<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_influence">Political influence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAE_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Political influence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Former Foreign Secretary Robin Cook said of his time in office that he "came to learn that the chairman of BAE appeared to have the key to the garden door to number 10. Certainly I never knew No 10 to come up with any decision which would be incommoding to BAE."<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>  As well as employing in-house lobbyists, BAE Systems also employs a lobbying agency called <a href="/wiki/Portland_Communications" title="Portland Communications">Portland PR</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> many of Portland PR\'s staff have worked at the upper echelons of both Labour and Conservative governments.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
